  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_59ee33e2-af70-4eab-85a9-e8c3446d0e86'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1833933989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9129525662712981923">This was pretty good. I definitely enjoyed "D.Gray-man" waaay more than I thought I would. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3227766081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3227766081" />
    <a title="Nocturnalux" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18314688-nocturnalux"><img alt="Nocturnalux" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457118068p2/18314688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3227766081?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nocturnalux" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nocturnalux" href="/user/show/18314688-nocturnalux">Nocturnalux</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9784088736914" href="/book/show/569436.D_Gray_man_1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18314688-nocturnalux?shelf=manga-in-japanese">manga-in-japanese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3227766081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8215292611896619116">There was a time when <b>D.Gray Man</b> was all the rage. An often cheap but still compelling anime adaptation that aired between 2006-2008 brought a lot of attention to Hoshino-sensei and for a while the franchise was immensely popular. But after a long hiatus (due to a bizarre health crisis in the <i>mangaka</i>'s life that may be addressed at a later point) the furor died out and by the time a sequel to the anime rolled by in 2016 it went by almost unheeded. <br/><br/>This is quite unfortunate as this is a solid <i>sho</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8215292611896619116" style="display:none">There was a time when <b>D.Gray Man</b> was all the rage. An often cheap but still compelling anime adaptation that aired between 2006-2008 brought a lot of attention to Hoshino-sensei and for a while the franchise was immensely popular. But after a long hiatus (due to a bizarre health crisis in the <i>mangaka</i>'s life that may be addressed at a later point) the furor died out and by the time a sequel to the anime rolled by in 2016 it went by almost unheeded. <br /><br />This is quite unfortunate as this is a solid <i>shounen</i> title that is considerably superior, in my opinion, to many other more successful manga. Alas, such are the fickle ways of the 2D industry (and I speak for the Western reception first and foremost as I am not up to date to what Japanese readers think) but be it as it may, the manga is still running and as yet to be canceled so there must be a large enough fanbase to make it viable in the highly competitive world of battle/adventure manga.<br /><br />This first volume is a good introduction to the 'imaginary 19th century' where the story takes place. Via aesthetics that are very reminiscent of Tim Burton at his best, <b>D.Gray Man</b> unfolds pop Gothic visuals, for lack of a better term, with Catholic imagery galore (to the point a cross is embedded in the main's hand), while opting for a strong contrast between black and white spaces that works very well in giving it a graphic look. Interestingly, shaded panels almost always point to dreamy sequences, at times of a quasi-symbolic nature, in which the villain tempts people into crossing a line they should not.<br /><br />This villain is the Millenium Earl, a figure that is most remarkable in terms of how he is visually represented. The Earl is very fat, drawn in a more simpler style than the rest of the cast, and could have stepped out from virtually any (good) Tim Burton movie. With absurdly tiny glasses, a bizarrely long mouth that is almost the entire face and a very tall hat perched precariously on his head as he skips about with a pumpkin topped umbrella, he looks more like comic relief than anything else. But that is a very big mouth indeed and it is full of teeth. <br /><br />The Earl is so unique a figure that it makes perfect sense that he should make it to the cover of the very first volume, right next to Allen, the main. In a sense, the Earl's dual nature of buffoon and terrifying monster with the power to manipulate people when they are at their lowest is the essence of the entire manga: it has its moments of comedy but is much, much darker than one might assume.<br /><br />Almost right away we learn about the nature of the Earl's weapon of choice, the Akuma. I will spoiler-tag it as first time readers may not want to know: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[These are created by attaching the soul to a mechanical skeleton via a loved one calling it back from the land of the dead (or something to that effect, it is not entirely clear how the afterlife functions); once animated the now trapped soul is a slave to the Earl who gets it to kill the loved one and impersonate them by using the now dead human body as a skin mask of sorts. It is absolutely chilling and the way it is shown enough to give one the creeps: the skeleton lowers its spine into the host body by the mouth. The Akuma now looks like a human and is free to mingle and kill. The more an Akuma kills, the more it evolves and the more dangerous it becomes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Arguably, the process of Akuma creation is a bit convoluted and this volume goes through it twice but it is at the core of what makes <b>D.Gray Man</b> more than your average battle manga. There is real human drama here and already in the first chapters it gets presented in all its horror. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It comes as no surprise that Allen himself turned his adoptive father into an Akuma after his death but it gives him a kind of motivation few <i>shounen</i> heroes can equal. His Innocence weapon slashing Mana against Allen's will is the stuff of nightmares and one that the manga knows how to use to its full advantage as the story progresses. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Allen is a very likable character and one of the few <i>shounen</i> heroes I do not abhor. In this volume he displays the typical skill set of great power, courage and desire to improve at all costs. But he is not rash or annoying even if he very much the 'gotta save them all' type that I tend to really not care for. Perhaps it is because the world of <b>D.Gray Man</b> is so dark and each loss ends up resonating all across, including one-chapter characters, that his savior strike becomes so compelling.<br />Or maybe I just like white haired <i>bishies</i>.<br /><br />On that subject, <b>D.Gray Man</b> is a manga that is <i>shounen</i> in spirit but veers on <i>shoujo</i> visually. It is a combination that I favor and here it is impeccable. Interestingly enough, the character design shifted to less suave in the anime: this is all the more visible in Kanda who, in the manga, could very well pass for a female character but comes across as much more masculine in the anime adaptation (especially <b>Hallow</b>, the later one). But there is a complicated history regarding the artwork that will be covered at another time. <br /><br />The battles themselves are intense and convey a sense of movement with grace but Hoshino is still perfecting her craft. When Allen goes against several Akuma simultaneously some of the flow is lost and one is not entirely sure of what is happening. <br /><br />Said battles revolve around Allen's weapon, a left arm that is normally red and borderline deformed but morphs into an impressive shining claw when activated. It is here that the before mentioned cross is embedded so the symbolical appeal is unmistakable even as the manga evolves toward a greater and more complex sense of nuance. <br /><br />I had read this before in English but this was my first time reading this particular manga in Japanese. I feel like an idiot for never having figured out before that Kanda's blade, 'Mugen' is written as [六幻] ('six illusions') and not [無限] ('infinity'); the homophone is deliberate but given than Kanda calls out his attacks as 'first illusion' and so forth, I should have realized it but it never even crossed my mind. <br /><br />To my great surprise, I was able to read this in two goes across two days. That is a record for me and while it may seem a petty one, I am still quite proud of myself, <i>furigana</i> not withstanding. With that said, I still struggled to make heads or tails of the handwritten parts. It never ceases to baffle me how <i>mangaka</i>, who draw for a living, can have such untidy and borderline illegible handwriting (or why manga insist in printing them as such as opposed to just using regular characters) with the occasional missing stroke. Native Japanese speakers and very advanced learners do not need all strokes to figure it out but I do like my <i>kanji</i> to be complete. <br /><br />Revisiting this manga allowed to fully appreciate it. I had found myself thinking, as I watched later episodes of the anime, that at some point the story lost coherence and went in contradictory directions. But I now realize that what seemed almost random plot decisions on the part of <i>sensei</i> were in fact a long game: Hoshino was foreshadowing almost from the very first panel and she knew very well what she was doing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8215292611896619116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_169020158" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169020158" />
    <a title="John Egbert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5223517-john-egbert"><img alt="John Egbert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340483284p2/5223517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169020158?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Egbert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Egbert" href="/user/show/5223517-john-egbert">John Egbert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERY LIVING BREATHING CREATURE ON THIS EARTH</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to John by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-">Jillian -always aspiring-</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5223517-john-egbert?shelf=omfg-it-s-a-series">omfg-it-s-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5223517-john-egbert?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5223517-john-egbert?shelf=oh-mah-god">oh-mah-god</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169020158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5710291537241746066">Note: This is half a review of the whole series...so it is very confusing at times...incredibly confusing and I don't stop to explain myself, not once, so continue at your own peril. In fact, no, don't read this because it's actually a pretty bad review I'll probably edit/delete later. Bye!<br/><br/><br/>Screw this. I'm writing this review right now, no more procrastinating for Mello, yup! And after this I'm going to write my review of Hetalia! AND AFTER THAT I WILL WORK ON MY NANOWRIMO NOVEL!<br/><br/>Well, okay, maybe</span>
  <span id="freeText5710291537241746066" style="display:none">Note: This is half a review of the whole series...so it is very confusing at times...incredibly confusing and I don't stop to explain myself, not once, so continue at your own peril. In fact, no, don't read this because it's actually a pretty bad review I'll probably edit/delete later. Bye!<br><br><br>Screw this. I'm writing this review right now, no more procrastinating for Mello, yup! And after this I'm going to write my review of Hetalia! AND AFTER THAT I WILL WORK ON MY NANOWRIMO NOVEL!<br><br>Well, okay, maybe not exactly in that order. I'll probably procrastinate and loaf around for a long time. And then I'll read more of Homestruck and complain about how long it is. Yup.<br><br>But, regardless, let's get on with this review, shall we?<br><br>Okay, D Gray Man. What can I say? I LOVE D GRAY MAN. It is and will always be my favorite manga, but even I have to admit it has it's flaws.<br><br>Although I for one was drawn in this volume from the very beginning and could not put it down (Come on guys! Allen had a cat in this volume! A CAATTTS!) I can see how it may be...dull...to others.<br><br>(Inner trollish Mello: WUT HOW COUDL U SAY THINGS LIEK DAT ABOUT D GRAY MANN?!)<br><br>Because, inner trollish Mello, I am sensible Mello and I can see that even my favorite series has flaws.<br><br>For instance, many compare D Gray Man to Fullmetal Alchemist. At first I didn't really see the similarities. lol, I mean we're talking about this guy:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380350035i/703953.png" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Versus <i>this</i> guy:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380350035i/703954.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However...as time progressed I began to see the similarities...<br><br>Allen and Edward...<br><br>...both have fucked up arms...<br><br>...both have fucked up arms as result of parent's deaths...<br><br>...both have crazy as shit mechanics (look, Komui, I love you, but you are clearly crazy)...<br><br>...both have dead parents...<br><br>...both have tried to resurrect dead parents only for it to end up HOLY CRAP TOTALLY WRONG...<br><br>...both are criminally short...<br><br>...and are picked on constantly for this...<br><br>...and always take offense at being picked on constantly for this...<br><br>Yeah, well, I won't go on and on. The point is that on the surface...D Gray Man may not seem...<i>terribly</i> original.<br><br>BUT BUT BUT BUT BUT<br><br>WAITTT!<br><br>Okay, look, that's just on the surface. I personally didn't mind the severe lack of...plot...*cringes* (I really don't want to say lack of plot, because that's not entirely it, but...) because I fell in love (no, not literally) with Allen (yes, okay, literally). <br><br>Really, D Gray Man as a whole has never been strong with plot...well, except for the place we're at the series as I type this sentence. Hoshino is a master storyteller, at least at the moment, in fact she's always been a master storyteller, she's just not all that fantastic with the plot in the middle. But that was fine, at least for me, because I loved the characters so much I was willing to read anything about them.<br><br>Basically...yeah, okay, you read this volume and no...it's not all <i>that</i> spectacular. But later it starts to develop more clearly, we are introduced to major characters, the plot thickens (well, uh, I would hold my horses on that one, but...) and everything picks up! But just not here. Here Hoshino introduced us to all of the terms she'd be using (Akuma, Excorcist, Innocence...something else?) and that was kind of a mistake. She needed a stronger way to pull in readers. But that's not the point. Well, actually it is.<br><br>ARGH WHAT DO I HAVE TO DO TO CONVINCE YOU TO READ D GRAY MAN!<br><br>I can't seem to say anything that doesn't come out sounding overtly critical of it!<br><br>Okay, you know what, let me tell you <i>my</i> reasons for sticking with D Gray Man all this time, maybe that will help?<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380350035i/703955._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The team dynamic Hoshino uses!<br><br>It's flawless! Well, maybe I shouldn't say that just incase there is a flaw I figure out sometime in the future. But right now I will say it: it's flawless! I love everyone on the team, nobody's lagging anyone else behind unlike on the Naruto team where there was always annoying Sakura, and, uh, IT'S A GOOD TEAM DYNAMIC OKAY?<br><br>...I suck, terribly.<br><br>But let's move on from that depressing tidbit of the day!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380350035i/703956.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Uh...wait...wrong picture ._.'<br><br>Sorry Krory, but you're not exactly the reason I kept reading, sorry to say...I love Krory too, really, but...no.<br><br>HERE'S WHY!<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380350035i/703957.png" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>*makes small choking sound*<br><br>W-wait! Let me explain!<br><br>Firstly, let me just say that no, I am not a yaoi fangirl. Seriously. It's just, well, Laven is my one true pairing. IT'S PRACTICALLY CANON, AND I AM A CANON PURIST SO DON'T TAKE THAT LIGHTLY. I don't believe in throwing two people together just for the sake of it, but <i>LavixAllen works</i>. It just does! I mean, for chrissakes, they are all over each other half the time! And what about that hug, and-and...*mumbles*<br><br>Okay...so I am in this partly for my pairing.<br><br>...<br><br>...<br><br>...<br><br>...you'll never read it now, will you?<br><br>Look, it's not just that. I feel that the world building is weird, but once again it just works. The Exorcists, I love all of them. Lenalee isn't treated as a second class citizen (she's the girl of the team). Although some would argue that she's just fanservice because of her skirt, well, no. She actually has a personality that's visible, and hey, there is actually a halfway excuse for the skirt? (To be able to use her magical boots (please, please, don't ask me about that -_-') she needs as much leg space as possible.)<br><br>But, well, let me tell you something else...it's the powers.<br><br>All the powers, villains and heroes, are very, very confusing. Only if you're naive like me will you try to argue that they make sense, and as you can see not even I try and argue that they make sense. I won't even try to explain it here, in fact, just do a wiki search and save both of us the trouble. All I can say is that at least nobody's incredibly over powered by anyone else. Their power levels are always kept in check, and that's relief.<br><br>Uhhh...I think I may have went off point for the eighth or so time.<br><br>I'll end this review now.<br><br>TL;DR: THIS VOLUME MAY NOT SEEM LIKE MUCH BUT IT GETS BETTER AND THEN IT GETS A LITTLE WORSE AND THEN IT GETS A HELL OF A LOT BETTER AGAIN AND YOU BECOME ADDICTED. LIKE ME. DA END.</span>

<div id="review_226397089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226397089" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226397089?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226397089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5258835183807739135">Confession: I have a lot of problems with manga as a medium. It's actually surprising to me when I genuinely get into a manga series, because there are so many obstacles: I find the panels often confusing; it takes me several minutes to get used to reading right to left; I'm continually frustrated by the melodrama which plagues the beginning of most series and the way things are repeated over and over and over and over and over. So I guess my problem with this volume is not really with it, persa</span>
  <span id="freeText5258835183807739135" style="display:none">Confession: I have a lot of problems with manga as a medium. It's actually surprising to me when I genuinely get into a manga series, because there are so many obstacles: I find the panels often confusing; it takes me several minutes to get used to reading right to left; I'm continually frustrated by the melodrama which plagues the beginning of most series and the way things are repeated over and over and over and over and over. So I guess my problem with this volume is not really with it, persay, as with the fact that it falls prey to so many genre weaknesses.<br /><br />The basic concept is interesting - fascinating, even. A war between the forces of good - armed with something nebulously called 'Innocence' - and those of evil with a horde of half machine/half tortured human soul weapons at their disposal is a really cool idea. Unfortunately... it feels to me a lot like Claymore. The protagonist, Allen Walker, seems to be a similar sort of mysterious not-quite-human/almost-the-enemy type as all Claymores. Actually, he strikes me as the combination of a Claymore and Edward Elric - and ergo he doesn't feel to me like something new.<br /><br />I think I would have given this book four stars if it hadn't been for the constant repetition of the word 'akuma'. Surely, surely, if these things have been around for ages they have more than one name. Surely, even if they don't, it's not necessary to use it so often. Pronouns, people, pronouns! They weren't invented just for shits and giggles! Use them!<br /><br />Other than that... hmm. Well, there are things that deserve dramatic reveals with exclamation points. It helps if these things are not the same things which characters have explained very calmly the page before.<br /><br />I'm not going to give up on the series yet, but I'm not in a hurry to track it down after this less-than-stunning opener.<br /><br />(P.S. Millenium Earl = Rasputin? Spoil for me.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5258835183807739135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_182733995" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182733995" />
    <a title="Zoe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5753804-zoe"><img alt="Zoe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483305583p2/5753804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182733995?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe" href="/user/show/5753804-zoe">Zoe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182733995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1249692453037833095">D.Gray-Man (the author has said that the title has nothing to do with the series - it was picked because it sounded cool) is one of the strangest manga's that I've encountered thus far. It's sort of a cross between a Tim Burton movie, the best of the steampunk/horror genre, with a few elements of Victorian England thrown in. Its art style is just as strange - the characters are drawn in a very specific way; you either love it or hate it. <br/>Onto the plot: <br/>Allen Walker is cursed. He tried to bring h</span>
  <span id="freeText1249692453037833095" style="display:none">D.Gray-Man (the author has said that the title has nothing to do with the series - it was picked because it sounded cool) is one of the strangest manga's that I've encountered thus far. It's sort of a cross between a Tim Burton movie, the best of the steampunk/horror genre, with a few elements of Victorian England thrown in. Its art style is just as strange - the characters are drawn in a very specific way; you either love it or hate it. <br />Onto the plot: <br />Allen Walker is cursed. He tried to bring his adoptive father back to life with the aid of the mysterious Millennium Earl (who may or may not have rabbit ears), only to end up with an eye that can see Akuma - demons created by the Millennium Earl who are under his control. He was born with a deformed arm, with a strange green cross embedded in it: he later finds out that this is his 'Innocence,' an elusive substance that Exorcists (those chosen by God to slay Akuma) wield as their main weapon. He learns of the race to collect all of the Innocence before the Earl; unless the Exorcists win, he will surely dominate the entire world.<br /><br />D.Gray-Man has gotten a lot of flack for having a bit of a coordination problem when it comes to fight scenes (it's hard to tell what the heck is going on sometimes), but the art is beautiful and the characters enchanting. Allen is a first-class sweetie (no, guys, that is NOT a reason for you not to read the series! Someone can be sweet-natured and tough at the same time!), Lavi is charmingly funny, Komui is hilariously messy, and Lenalee (just about the only female character in the series) is cute and tough at the same time: a good combination in a shonen series. <br />While D.Gray-Man isn't that well known, it deserves to be. So hurry up and buy/borrow these books and give it the reputation it deserves! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1249692453037833095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Selena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3855249-selena"><img alt="Selena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325469161p2/3855249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106457624?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Selena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Selena" href="/user/show/3855249-selena">Selena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=my-must-reads">my-must-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=manga-manwha">manga-manwha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=japan-stuff">japan-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=first-in-series-manga">first-in-series-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=timey-wimey">timey-wimey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=cats">cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=magic">magic</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106457624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15427226728232104554">Rereading the first volume after having followed this series for more than a decade is a bit of a trip.<br/><br/>So much stuff was in this first volume that never gets addressed again, but while the details have definitely changed over the years (or have they?), the premise remains constant.<br/><br/>Allen Walker is an exorcist with a hand that becomes a weapon to defeat monsters called "Akuma." This first volume is him traveling to join up with The Black Order, a group devoted to destroying Akuma, defeating the Mi</span>
  <span id="freeText15427226728232104554" style="display:none">Rereading the first volume after having followed this series for more than a decade is a bit of a trip.<br /><br />So much stuff was in this first volume that never gets addressed again, but while the details have definitely changed over the years (or have they?), the premise remains constant.<br /><br />Allen Walker is an exorcist with a hand that becomes a weapon to defeat monsters called "Akuma." This first volume is him traveling to join up with The Black Order, a group devoted to destroying Akuma, defeating the Millennium Earl, and collecting pieces of a mysterious substance called "Innocence." He gets sidetracked on his trip for most of this volume, but the little vignettes help build Allen as a character and get the relevant story information out there before we dive into the meat of the series.<br /><br />Admittedly, this first volume is more info-dump than I remember it being the first time I read it, but enough is happening to intersperse the overload of information with battles and back story for our hero. The art is pretty terrible in most of it, but in a charming "I'm trying, watch me grow" kind of way (seriously, later volumes of this series are gorgeously gothic).<br /><br />This volume is a middle-of-the-road start for one of my favorite series of all time. It was enough to get me invested all those years ago, and I recommend giving it a shot. If the first volume has you intrigued, there's a lot of awesome waiting for you down the road.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15427226728232104554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3544768133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Greg Markwardt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10528447-greg-markwardt"><img alt="Greg Markwardt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380635208p2/10528447.jpg" /></a>

        rated it

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9246589096748038986">Ah yes, I still love this series, I know I saw about 50 episodes of it long time ago, and also read some volumes of the manga, but I never finished. This was just so good. Happy to see Allen again. <br/><br/>I decided to re-read this one, I didn’t really want to start a big book right before my vacation, and also all the books I really wanted to read are now boxed up and ready for my vacation (yes, I am writing this review before my vacation starts).<br/><br/>In this one we first meet with Allen, we find out about </span>
  <span id="freeText9246589096748038986" style="display:none">Ah yes, I still love this series, I know I saw about 50 episodes of it long time ago, and also read some volumes of the manga, but I never finished. This was just so good. Happy to see Allen again. <br /><br />I decided to re-read this one, I didn’t really want to start a big book right before my vacation, and also all the books I really wanted to read are now boxed up and ready for my vacation (yes, I am writing this review before my vacation starts).<br /><br />In this one we first meet with Allen, we find out about his history, about why he looks the way he does (though I am sure there is more backstory in the future, as there are still enough questions left), we also see him travel around to get to the Black Order, while his master is once again on the run (which always makes me laugh, though I also feel sorry for Allen that he is stuck to such an eccentric master).<br /><br />I loved seeing Allen travel, and also do some exorcism stuff. He meets some people who I hope we will meet again in the future. I did feel sorry for the people he met, and their circumstances. I can’t imagine how much it must hurt to find out your loved one, or your friend is an Akuma. <br /><br />The Earl was creepy as I remembered him, and I can’t wait to read more about his backstory, we do find out some stuff, but the Earl is still a big fluff ball of mystery.<br /><br />The Black Order, and what happened there, I just laughed so much. Ah, Kanda being Kanda (pissy as always), Komui (an idiot as always, just loved how everyone was just sighing at the fact that he failed once again), and we also meet other characters. It sure was a delight to see everyone again, and to see Allen truly start his exorcist job.<br /><br />The art is really pretty, and I just love how everyone is drawn, but I also love all the little details that are scattered through the pages. &lt;3<br /><br />All in all, I will be sure to read more of this manga, I am not sure if I will write a review for each of these volumes though. Maybe for a few or maybe I will bundle them.<br /><br />Review first posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twirlingbookprincess.com">https://twirlingbookprincess.com</a></span>

<div id="review_445633479" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445633479" />
    <a title="Emma Adams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9368102-emma-adams"><img alt="Emma Adams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461063549p2/9368102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445633479?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Adams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Adams" href="/user/show/9368102-emma-adams">Emma Adams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9368102-emma-adams?shelf=supernatural-and-horror">supernatural-and-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9368102-emma-adams?shelf=manga-and-comics">manga-and-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9368102-emma-adams?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445633479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16192798534837927422">Sooo...this is probably my all-time favourite manga series. Where to start? Well, the story follows Allen Walker, an Exorcist - one of those chosen by a divine substance called Innocence to fight against the sinister Millennium Earl, who steals human souls to make demons known as Akuma. Only Exorcists can fight Akuma and it seems like a futile battle from the outset – the number of Akuma is potentially infinite, whereas the Exorcists are a small group scattered across the globe.<br/><br/>Some of this soun</span>
  <span id="freeText16192798534837927422" style="display:none">Sooo...this is probably my all-time favourite manga series. Where to start? Well, the story follows Allen Walker, an Exorcist - one of those chosen by a divine substance called Innocence to fight against the sinister Millennium Earl, who steals human souls to make demons known as Akuma. Only Exorcists can fight Akuma and it seems like a futile battle from the outset – the number of Akuma is potentially infinite, whereas the Exorcists are a small group scattered across the globe.<br /><br />Some of this sound familiar? Aha – it’s deceptive, because Katsura Hoshino completely turns expectations on their head. The first time I read a few volumes, I thought, OK, this is pretty good. But it took a second reading to really get the brilliance of it – and it gets better the further in you get. Trust me.<br /><br />I love the creepy, dark gothic vibe. I love that it’s set in an alternative nineteenth century in which sinister cyberpunk-esque demons, Akuma, are an accepted fact of life. The Millennium Earl is hands-down one of the best villains I’ve ever read – I mean, look at him. He carries a talking umbrella/golem called Lero, by the way. Yeah. That’s another thing I love about this manga – the bizarre randomness that balances all the tragedy. The Akuma come from the souls of dead humans, trapped in a form that makes them kill their loved ones – as you can imagine, there are some damn near heart-breaking moments. But there’s a lot of humour, too. <br /><br />The characters…well, we have Allen, cursed by his own father, who he resurrected as an Akuma. Allen can now see the soul of any human trapped within an Akuma, as well as bearing a cross embedded in his hand that gives him the power to vanquish the demons. He has a tragic history but is almost maddeningly optimistic, always smiling. We meet Allen in this volume, but not many of the other awesome characters we get to know later on. I'll avoid spoilers and just say that D.Gray-Man is witty, fun, wonderfully dark and creepy – everything I love to read!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16192798534837927422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2751247439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2751247439" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28600218-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507081132p2/28600218.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2751247439?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/28600218-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28600218-bradley?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2751247439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer216595377554740559"> I think this series was incredibly popular while I was in high school. Late to the show. <br/><br/> Popular in my day? It could run popular now. The enemies, called Akuma, are literally a physical manifestation of the darkness in one’s heart. The souls need help when coming back to this world unwillingly and that’s where our villain, the Millenium Earl, comes in. It’s described in several ways and in different ways which makes it foolproof even when it might not seem completely aligned…For instance it’s </span>
  <span id="freeText216595377554740559" style="display:none"> I think this series was incredibly popular while I was in high school. Late to the show. <br /><br /> Popular in my day? It could run popular now. The enemies, called Akuma, are literally a physical manifestation of the darkness in one’s heart. The souls need help when coming back to this world unwillingly and that’s where our villain, the Millenium Earl, comes in. It’s described in several ways and in different ways which makes it foolproof even when it might not seem completely aligned…For instance it’s also noted that Akuma are programmed weapons using a soul, machine and tragedy. Why am I expounding on this? Because it’s good world building!<br /> <br /> Allen Walker, our main protagonist, is not some inflated jockey who has been training nonsensically all of their life (he does have a mentor, but you get the point). Allen is a victim. He helps people by defeating Akuma, but the wake of that destruction is left for people to bare. This feels much like an allegory for depression and anxiety. I could be forcing that one on here as I went to a community conversation about just that yesterday.<br /><br /> It’s the theme that made this popular so I don’t think I am too far off the mark. High schoolers, or any young teens/adults might not be able to articulate it or they are simply in denial that they sucked this up as a translation for how they feel…For how things are.<br /><br /> I enjoyed <i>D. Gray-man</i>. The protagonist is amiable in ways that are not annoying and its set in a world that rings with Gothic imagery but to me seemed quite ordinary. I wouldn’t mind continuing this series.<br /><br /> I’m on a quest to clear out a bunch of manga that I have only the first volume of and I’m creating two piles of those I will continue and those I am sending to the library. Here’s to continuing!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="216595377554740559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13535669697153504268">~3.5 Stars~<br/><br/>I found this in a used/new bookstore in Bangor, Maine, and I decided, well - I watched the first episode of the anime forever ago and I remember it wasn't too bad, so... why not? Turned out it was a good idea, because I ended up running out of books on the way back to ND, and also because... it wasn't bad!<br/><br/>As far as I can tell, this is a fairly popular manga series. Or at least, it was back when I was first getting into manga and mostly just reading Bleach. Either way, I can pretty muc</span>
  <span id="freeText13535669697153504268" style="display:none">~3.5 Stars~<br /><br />I found this in a used/new bookstore in Bangor, Maine, and I decided, well - I watched the first episode of the anime forever ago and I remember it wasn't too bad, so... why not? Turned out it was a good idea, because I ended up running out of books on the way back to ND, and also because... it wasn't bad!<br /><br />As far as I can tell, this is a fairly popular manga series. Or at least, it was back when I was first getting into manga and mostly just reading Bleach. Either way, I can pretty much see why. It's engaging, the main character is one I like, and... it kind of reminds me of Black Butler. So I can see why it would be popular. <br /><br />The series follows Allen Walker, an exorcist. It takes place in the 19th century - obviously fictionalized, as the manga vehemently tells us. Several times. The artwork is nice, there are definite creepy parts, also Yuu Kanda. <br /><br />So, yeah. I'll probably pick up later volumes in this series and I'll probably watch the anime at some point, but it's not high priority right now. It was decent! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13535669697153504268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13276903867050087738">I took some time to get used to its artwork. The magic system looks familiar actually, having a weapon planted on the main character, Allen's body, and he was cursed. Another very typical shounen manga, but I'm intrigued with its execution, heard great things about it and the series is continued by the mangaka after a few years, that's rare. This gave me some fullmetal alchemist vibe tbh, but I don't mind if the artwork and plot get better after this. Hope to read more of this soon! 3 stars!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8761516500476246983">"Exorcists...those possessed by the gods...they exist to destroy the ominous evils that rise from the darkness."<br/><br/>Disappearances at a church catch the interest of Mou and Charles who bring two policemen with them, advancing into the abandoned church to find out the explanation for all the weird occurrences.<br/><br/>The plot thickens when the four come to realise they are not alone, as a 15-year-old boy explains the church is inhabited by an Akuma.<br/><br/>Enter Allen Walker, escorted into the police station under s</span>
  <span id="freeText8761516500476246983" style="display:none">"Exorcists...those possessed by the gods...they exist to destroy the ominous evils that rise from the darkness."<br /><br />Disappearances at a church catch the interest of Mou and Charles who bring two policemen with them, advancing into the abandoned church to find out the explanation for all the weird occurrences.<br /><br />The plot thickens when the four come to realise they are not alone, as a 15-year-old boy explains the church is inhabited by an Akuma.<br /><br />Enter Allen Walker, escorted into the police station under suspicion as a suspect in the death of one of the officers. While under questioning, Allen explains the thing in the church was an Akuma and the more it kills, the more powerful it grows. He lets them see the cross embedded in his reddened hand, telling them it is an anti-Akuma weapon used in his exorcisms.<br /><br />Allen knows only too well about the ultra dangerous Millenium Earl who controls the Akuma, a being which is a combination of soul and machine.<br /><br />On a perilous journey, he reaches the exorcist headquarters of the Black Order, a huge, looming tower on top of a cliff. Once there he has to gain entry by proving he is not an Akuma, which is difficult as he bears the pentacle of one doomed soul.<br /><br />Hoshino Katsura has brought a unique and mysterious world to life in the pages of this series. Exorcists and demons battle in a really fun good versus evil series of matches that will leave the reader satisfied, though there is more to this than meets the eye.<br /><br />Allen Walker has a hidden past but is a good exorcist, the Millenium Earl creates and uses the scourge demons Akuma while a troop of exorcists from the Black Order team up with him to defeat their kind from getting an unhealthy grasp on humanity.<br /><br />There is much detail in the artwork, as much as there are many aspects to the storyline.<br />This will be enjoyed by those who already like Bleach and Zombie Powder.</span>

  <span id="freeText1803708605327206397" style="display:none">Did this come out around same time as Full Metal Alchemist? I was instantly enjoying the main character and was actually shocked how fast certain characters died or were taken out. I believe that helped pushed my enjoyment on something that's done before. A 3 out of 5. </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_243009441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/243009441" />
    <a title="Petros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6984857-petros"><img alt="Petros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321523871p2/6984857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/243009441?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petros" href="/user/show/6984857-petros">Petros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer243009441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8149625857959433778">ART SECTION: 8/10<br/>The gothic motif is something worthy of praise, while the rather rough outlines make everything look more grim and scary. Besides that, like almost any other shounen it is full of rather clear-cut good guys and bad guys, dressed in clothes following a motif. So aesthetics aside it plays out as any other of its kind. Still, those decorations around the Gothic world were quite catchy.<br/><br/>STORY SECTION: 4/10 <br/><br/>The initial chapters are marvelous and really attract your attention. It is ab</span>
  <span id="freeText8149625857959433778" style="display:none">ART SECTION: 8/10<br />The gothic motif is something worthy of praise, while the rather rough outlines make everything look more grim and scary. Besides that, like almost any other shounen it is full of rather clear-cut good guys and bad guys, dressed in clothes following a motif. So aesthetics aside it plays out as any other of its kind. Still, those decorations around the Gothic world were quite catchy.<br /><br />STORY SECTION: 4/10 <br /><br />The initial chapters are marvelous and really attract your attention. It is about an alternative Earth, full of gothic motifs, where an evil demon/ghost of sorts plans to destroy it by exploiting peoples’ grief over the death of their loved ones, luring them to raise the dead and thus creating monsters that kill innocents and sink the world into chaos. The heroes have to find Innocence, powers that protect the world, and battle the Evil Earl and his minions.<br /><br />Such formula is more than familiar for a shounen series, but the interesting twist is that this happens in a Gothic world. Monsters are created and heroes gain power-ups in many shounen series; although here it feels somewhat less obvious as the monsters are made from love and innocence may hurt even bystanders. This is usually enough to keep the average viewer watching. The first dozen of episodes are just fine, introducing the main characters, their sad lives, the secret organization that was made to stop the Earl and the objective goals of each side.<br /><br />The problem comes right after the basic plot and cast are presented. Typical to its genre, the characters behave in predictable shounen manner and the battles are full of power-ups, where they didn’t really need them to progress the story. I mean, giving the monsters level ups was ok the first time, as it was giving them individuality and personality (like Menos Grande in Bleach). But thereafter, it was just lame; leveling up for the sake of leveling up. Plus, the good guys typically gain extra power right when they want it, so it lost its suspense quite soon.<br /><br />There is no conclusion and the manga is pretty much abandoned by its maker, a sign of how even she got bored of its cheesy development. So, you are basically left with an abandoned unoriginal story with a good main idea. But wait, even the nice idea is not that nice if you look around. There has been a weird Gothic manga motif fad going around, so many manga seem to have the same feeling lately. <br /><br />CHARACTER SECTION: 5/10 <br /><br />I’m not going into many details because down to it, if you have read some Jump shounen, you know exactly what to expect. A pretty, kind-hearted boy as lead with a superpower that beats everything, a pretty girl as support, some other dudes as antagonists and sidekicks and the sort. The good guys are all young, yet have superpowers that level buildings and that is no surprise for this genre and thus not a minus. Seriously, the cast is quite typical for its genre; it pains even more to see that they hardly develop any further than the initial episodes they appear in. Or some flashbacks that simply explain their sad past and present role in the organization. And as always, power-ups don’t count as development.<br /><br />Even the villains look cool but you hardly get to know anything about them, other than they just want to destroy the world. As for the monster minions, they are pretty much cannon fodder and you will lose interest in them a few seconds after they are defeated.<br /><br />All things considered, the characters are ok for such a series and they’re colorized to a generally high degree. But that is that and no more. They are not special, unique or even complete. Thus, I give them the base for being simply nice to watch.<br /><br />VALUE SECTION: 2/10 <br />Although there was plenty of hype around it when the series was circulating regularly, all the fame went away quite fast when a certain-other-similar-manga began to circulate, so it didn’t even manage to get some historical value. It WOULD have some if it was complete or if there wasn’t this Manga Gothic Fad going on right now. If you compare it to other shounen, it is quite one-of-the-same. If you compare it to other Goth manga, it is by far the less interesting in terms of atmosphere or story. So, the chances of rereading it or having a reason to remember it are few to none. <br /><br />ENJOYMENT SECTION: 4/10 <br />Besides the initial chapters and a few other ones here and there, this series felt generic and didn’t keep me very interested. So, I say go for the titles in my Suggestion List. They are very similar yet far more catchy.<br /><br />VERDICT: 4.5/10<br />Another shounen series, which had the potential to excel, but also went under because of its bad planning. And in far less chapters than Naruto or Bleach.<br /><br />SUGGESTION LIST<br />Soul Eater<br />Death Note<br />Bleach<br />Ao no Exorcist<br />Beelzebub</span>
  <a data-text-id="8149625857959433778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daichi Ishii" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daichi Ishii" href="/user/show/80369564-daichi-ishii">Daichi Ishii</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358851569" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2918926126547436074">It was really good! I learned that when we judge something, we have to think about it from various aspect. We face to situation which we recognize someone as a bad person because of their bad behavior but sometimes they have some reasons why they took bad behavior. This story has a lot of sad scene that somebody’s important parson is killed but it was fun.</span>

<div id="review_543235162" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/543235162" />
    <a title="MissAnnThrope" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526539-missannthrope"><img alt="MissAnnThrope" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379715677p2/1526539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/543235162?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MissAnnThrope" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MissAnnThrope" href="/user/show/1526539-missannthrope">MissAnnThrope</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526539-missannthrope?shelf=shonen">shonen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526539-missannthrope?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526539-missannthrope?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526539-missannthrope?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526539-missannthrope?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543235162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11325577546337674945"><i>22 February 2013</i><br/><br/><b>Rating: * * 1/2</b><br/><br/><i>D.Gray-Man: Opening, Vol. 1</i> starts off with a bang, but by the end of the volume it sort of fizzled out. The concept initially sounded intriguing, but the more I read on the more I kept thinking of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2880.Bleach__Volume_1_Strawberry_and_the_Soul_Reapers' title='Bleach, Volume 1 Strawberry and the Soul Reapers by Tite Kubo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bleach</a>. The akuma remind me of the tortured souls of the Hollows, and Allen Walker's curse seems similar to Ichigo's Soul Reaper powers. Some parts even brought to mind <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9876989.Blue_Exorcist__Vol__1' title='Blue Exorcist, Vol. 1 by Kazue Kato' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blue Exorcist</a>, which also has a Hogwarts-type school for exorcists. There's even a Snitch-like guide.<br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText11325577546337674945" style="display:none"><i>22 February 2013</i><br /><br /><b>Rating: * * 1/2</b><br /><br /><i>D.Gray-Man: Opening, Vol. 1</i> starts off with a bang, but by the end of the volume it sort of fizzled out. The concept initially sounded intriguing, but the more I read on the more I kept thinking of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2880.Bleach__Volume_1_Strawberry_and_the_Soul_Reapers" title="Bleach, Volume 1 Strawberry and the Soul Reapers by Tite Kubo" rel="nofollow noopener">Bleach</a>. The akuma remind me of the tortured souls of the Hollows, and Allen Walker's curse seems similar to Ichigo's Soul Reaper powers. Some parts even brought to mind <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9876989.Blue_Exorcist__Vol__1" title="Blue Exorcist, Vol. 1 by Kazue Kato" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Exorcist</a>, which also has a Hogwarts-type school for exorcists. There's even a Snitch-like guide.<br /><br />The artwork isn't bad, but again, it reminded me of other manga. Maybe I need to give demon/exorcist themed manga a break for a while. The art is a cross between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9876989.Blue_Exorcist__Vol__1" title="Blue Exorcist, Vol. 1 by Kazue Kato" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Exorcist</a> and the gothic bits of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6406018.Soul_Eater__Vol__1__Soul_Eater___1_" title="Soul Eater, Vol. 1 (Soul Eater, #1) by Atsushi Ohkubo" rel="nofollow noopener">Soul Eater</a>, but just not quite as good. <br /><br />Generally, I don't have an issue with manga having similarities because many of them cover the same themes. However, in order for me to be keep interest in the series, it must, at the very least, parallel the quality of those other great manga. If the story is strong enough, eventually it will stand out on its own and you stop making comparisons to the other books. Unfortunately, all I could do was think of all the other manga and it made me want to re-read those instead of continuing on with this series.<br /><br />Lately, I haven't been having much luck when I pick up a first volume to a series I am curious to read. The first volume fails to capture my interest enough to make me want to continue the series. Sometimes it takes a few volume to get a series going, so I may give <i>D.Gray-Man</i> another volume before I make any rash judgments on the series. I hope the next one is better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11325577546337674945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y+2SOFA1eJQaJ5kyYUskmXv/+f5lcvmXxno6dZossYaJxiq6rtk0M3nHa+jyv666CgPA/VAdK0+bqK+yhoZJiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ne6O1wmOV8+fXqHdmSYLEEvGg8idcA71f2LvvNPl5BnfxTZV92IbaPy+UwcK0oEzOjq6y6gf3C0isHp7z08cFA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer9919714896390109760"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4668338._' rel='nofollow noopener'>星野 桂</a><br/><br/>Katsura Hoshino ((星野 桂 Hoshino Katsura) was born on April 21, 1980, in Shiga Prefecture, Japan, as the younger of fraternal twin girls and the second of three children. She drew her first manga at twenty-one. In 1998, Hoshino moved to Tokyo. She dreamed of bringing her mother to the city and was able to in 2006.<br/><br/>She made her debut with her comics in July 2003 with the publication of her first m</span>
  <span id="freeText9919714896390109760" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4668338._" rel="nofollow noopener">星野 桂</a><br /><br />Katsura Hoshino ((星野 桂 Hoshino Katsura) was born on April 21, 1980, in Shiga Prefecture, Japan, as the younger of fraternal twin girls and the second of three children. She drew her first manga at twenty-one. In 1998, Hoshino moved to Tokyo. She dreamed of bringing her mother to the city and was able to in 2006.<br /><br />She made her debut with her comics in July 2003 with the publication of her first manga series Continue and is known for her work, D.Gray-man, which began serialization in Shueisha's Weekly Shōnen Jump in May 2004.</span>

  <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
